  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer225579226219230412"><b>A pulsating psycho-thriller from Ryu Murakami, author of <i>In the Miso Soup</i></b><br/><br/>A renaissance man for the postmodern age, Ryu Murakami—a musician, filmmaker (<i>Tokyo Decadence</i>), TV personality, and award-winning author—has gained a cult following in the West. His first novel, <i>Almost Transparent Blue</i>, won Japan’s most coveted literary prize and sold over a million copies, and his mo</span>
  <span id="freeText225579226219230412" style="display:none"><b>A pulsating psycho-thriller from Ryu Murakami, author of <i>In the Miso Soup</i></b><br /><br />A renaissance man for the postmodern age, Ryu Murakami—a musician, filmmaker (<i>Tokyo Decadence</i>), TV personality, and award-winning author—has gained a cult following in the West. His first novel, <i>Almost Transparent Blue</i>, won Japan’s most coveted literary prize and sold over a million copies, and his most recent psychosexual thriller, <i>In the Miso Soup</i>, gave readers a further taste of his incredibly agile imagination. In <i>Piercing</i>, Murakami, in his own unique style, explores themes of child abuse and what happens to the voiceless among us, weaving a disturbing, spare tale of two people who find each other and then are forced into hurting each other deeply because of the haunting specter of their own abuse as children.</span>
  <a data-text-id="225579226219230412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_2599770445" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2599770445" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2599770445?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2599770445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4873092351597297845">I could never be a nurse or a doctor or a paramedic. Thank GOD for those people, because they were born with a strength that I lack. The sight of blood, gore, bone, vomit, and any number of other bodily excretions, well, they make me lightheaded, wobbly-kneed. Don't get me started on the thought of parasites. Worms, they will be the death of me. Same with black flies (grown-up maggots!). In short, I'm a wimp.<br/><br/>I'm not wimpish when it comes to my literature, though. I love ruthless books, books tha</span>
  <span id="freeText4873092351597297845" style="display:none">I could never be a nurse or a doctor or a paramedic. Thank GOD for those people, because they were born with a strength that I lack. The sight of blood, gore, bone, vomit, and any number of other bodily excretions, well, they make me lightheaded, wobbly-kneed. Don't get me started on the thought of parasites. Worms, they will be the death of me. Same with black flies (grown-up maggots!). In short, I'm a wimp.<br /><br />I'm not wimpish when it comes to my literature, though. I love ruthless books, books that go places, sometimes deep and dark, sometimes extreme. They aren't frigid, these books. They don't employ restraint or propriety. They often disturb, chill, shock. They make my heart seize up a little, and I breathe, "YES" on the shaky exhale.<br /><br />But this book.<br /><br />It made me feel physically ill. It reminded me of the wimp I am when I'm in a hospital. Of how when I see blood, the edges become black as my consciousness threatens to slip away. The violence in this book forced me regularly to turn from the pages for a reprieve. But then I returned....<br /><br />I have to laugh at myself. What did I expect, anyway? The book's back cover explains that the main character has a visceral desire to stab his sleeping infant with an ice pick! Thankfully, he doesn't do it, but his way of avoiding it puts him in a completely different situation. A situation with an S&amp;M prostitute who is every bit as psychologically scarred as he is, and who desires to receive and inflict pain as much as he does. It is terrifying to see the extreme effects of their childhood trauma. It scared the shit out of me.<br /><br />Theirs is a psychotic understanding hopefully far too extreme for most readers to easily comprehend, but it does show how our damage can't help but leak out in harmful ways. Perhaps our ways don't result in a trip to the E.R., but they can wreak havoc all the same. <br /><br />Achilles' tendons. A Swiss Army knife. A can opener. An ice pick. An eye in its crimson world.<br /><br />God, we're a fucked up people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4873092351597297845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1051157142" />
    <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca"><img alt="Anthony Vacca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604067844p2/27183668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1051157142?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Vacca" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca">Anthony Vacca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anthony by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/13196983-lauren-floyd">Lauren Floyd</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051157142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10172580235663401900">Seriously perturbed about a rash of late-night impulses to murder his newborn child with an ice pick, Tokyo businessman Kawashima Masayuki decides that the only sensible thing to do is to murder a random prostitute instead. But even with all his careful preparations, which Kawashima painstakingly scribbles into a notebook, the last thing that our everyman hero expects is that his intended victim is just as deranged and volatile a freak as himself.<br/><br/>Sanada Chiaki is a S&M call girl in her early twe</span>
  <span id="freeText10172580235663401900" style="display:none">Seriously perturbed about a rash of late-night impulses to murder his newborn child with an ice pick, Tokyo businessman Kawashima Masayuki decides that the only sensible thing to do is to murder a random prostitute instead. But even with all his careful preparations, which Kawashima painstakingly scribbles into a notebook, the last thing that our everyman hero expects is that his intended victim is just as deranged and volatile a freak as himself.<br /><br />Sanada Chiaki is a S&amp;M call girl in her early twenties who has been suffering a sexual dry spell after a strand of unsatisfying boyfriends. When not lobotomizing herself on pharmaceuticals, Chiaki passes the time transferring the all-consuming inner turmoil of her deeply troubled past into acts of self-mutilation and occasional bodily harm to others.<br /><br /><i>Piercing</i> is a pithy and nasty novel with the structure and pacing of a shock-thriller until the narrative derails completely into a twisted romance (of sorts) between two psychotic, toxic personalities. After a deceivingly cursory set-up, the book shifts gears and the last hundred pages, which - in a single chapter - relates Kawashima and Chiaki's eventful night together, moves at some serious fucked-up velocity. And while bleak and certainly not for the weak of stomach, there is a mean-spirited streak of subtle gallows humor that penetrates the often erroneous interior dialogues of the novel's two leads, giving the novel dramatic heft as a disturbing satirical peep show into the psychogeography of the give and take and take and take that we call relationships.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10172580235663401900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2681538579?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meike" href="/user/show/59050228-meike">Meike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747593133" href="/book/show/830979.Piercing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681538579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15095293452994279202">Ryu Murakami is an expert on the high art of Japanese pulp - what's not to love? In this twisted thriller, two psychologically damaged characters are caught in a double standoff: They are fighting each other, and they are fighting the urge to self-destruct. And you could even make the case that the young father and the S/M sex worker aren't the only ones in the room, as they both suffer from out-of-body experiences caused by trauma and are haunted by their former tormentors - this novel has mult</span>
  <span id="freeText15095293452994279202" style="display:none">Ryu Murakami is an expert on the high art of Japanese pulp - what's not to love? In this twisted thriller, two psychologically damaged characters are caught in a double standoff: They are fighting each other, and they are fighting the urge to self-destruct. And you could even make the case that the young father and the S/M sex worker aren't the only ones in the room, as they both suffer from out-of-body experiences caused by trauma and are haunted by their former tormentors - this novel has multiple layers, one creepier than the other. <br /><br />Short intro to the story: Kawashima Masayuki is afraid he might hurt his own baby: Still terrorized by the abuse he endured from his mentally ill mother, he fights the impulse to stab his Infant with an ice pick - and he decides that in order to prevent this, he should stab a sex worker instead. But he didn't anticipate what this particular sex worker has in store for him...<br /><br />This book is wild, scary, and thrilling - a typical Ryu Murakami (and while I also love Haruki, I bet an unassuming reader who picks up this novel because he happened to confuse the two will be scarred for life! :-)). I'm on my way to become a Ryu completist, and I already have two more of his books on my bedside table: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17794325.From_the_Fatherland__with_Love" title="From the Fatherland, with Love by Ryū Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">From the Fatherland, with Love</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8032189.Popular_Hits_of_the_Showa_Era" title="Popular Hits of the Showa Era by Ryū Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Popular Hits of the Showa Era</a>.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2593867055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2593867055" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2593867055?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2593867055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7684433607822430600">Pain is collaborative. It has to be both inflicted and acknowledged, or it doesn't count. Ryu Murakami, the <a href='https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2011/02/07/popular-hits-of-the-showa-era' title='According to the New Yorker' rel='nofollow noopener'>"aging enfant terrible</a> of Japan," is interested in both. His work is marked by graphic sex and shocking violence. For some reason I saw the movie adaptation of his <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3392668-audition?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Audition</a> and I'm all set with piano wire now.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542676906i/26621491._SX540_.png' alt='piano' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Piano wire: it's not just for whatever it's supposed to be for!</i><br/><br/>The thing with relationships is that they constitute an agreement to inflict your damage on each other, right? "I am fuc</span>
  <span id="freeText7684433607822430600" style="display:none">Pain is collaborative. It has to be both inflicted and acknowledged, or it doesn't count. Ryu Murakami, the <a href="https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2011/02/07/popular-hits-of-the-showa-era" title="According to the New Yorker" rel="nofollow noopener">"aging enfant terrible</a> of Japan," is interested in both. His work is marked by graphic sex and shocking violence. For some reason I saw the movie adaptation of his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3392668-audition?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Audition</a> and I'm all set with piano wire now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542676906i/26621491._SX540_.png" alt="piano" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Piano wire: it's not just for whatever it's supposed to be for!</i><br><br>The thing with relationships is that they constitute an agreement to inflict your damage on each other, right? "I am fucked up and you're going to catch it, and you are fucked up and I'm going to catch it." And with any luck, you find someone who wants that kind of damage. Some people want to be controlled, some people want to control. Some people want to have big screaming fights, some people want more passive aggression in their lives. Romance is just matching damage. That's all we're talking about here in <i>Piercing.</i> I mean, my personal damage is, like, I make too many lists? And these people are both dangerously insane, so the scale is different. But still, basically same thing. I have this pain to give. I'd like it accepted. Acknowledged. <br><br>This is an icky thing to say! It's a pitch dark view of relationships. But there is a little bit of truth to it, isn't there? I thought about my marriage. It's perfect and my wife is my best friend and I love her all the way. But there's....there's not none of this, friend. There's a little damage. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542676828i/26621490.jpg" alt="murakami" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Ryu Murakami looking enfant terrible-y</i><br><br>One of the things you can do with fiction is take a human truth and blow it up to super dramatic size. It's what Bret Easton Ellis was up to in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242791704" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">American Psycho</a> and it's what Ryu Murakami is up to here, just as effectively. When writers go all the way into the dark, like Murakami does, they can force you to confront aspects of your own humanity that you'd maybe not always prefer to acknowledge. I think there's value in that.<br><br>Anyway, the very first image in <i>Piercing</i> is of a peacefully sleeping child, with his father standing over her crib in the night holding an ice pick up to her cheek. He's wondering what he can do to keep himself from stabbing her. He decides to murder a hooker instead, as one does. The hooker and he form a certain sort of relationship. Damage ensues! I accept it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7684433607822430600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681754595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3056231970166822455">The intersection of two very disturbed individuals exorcizes the reader's curiosity of how far a dangerous situation will go. Damaging childhood experiences and the resulting psychoses that drive each character's actions twist this novel upside down and through a warped looking-glass. This was my first novel by Ryu Murakami, and I look forward to my next foray into his dark recesses.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1601871275" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1601871275" />
    <a title="Emm C²" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c"><img alt="Emm C²" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558724665p2/53296236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1601871275?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emm C²" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emm C²" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c">Emm C²</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=adult-and-new-adult">adult-and-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1601871275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10371933274991294284"><i>This review and stranger things on <a href='https://bloodredvelvet.wordpress.com/category/book-reviews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood Red Velvet</a>.</i><br/><br/>Some books are unrelenting rays of sunshine, filling you with joy, optimism and hope for the future..... and then there is <i>Piercing</i>, a two-hundred-page miasma of darkness and human misery.<br/><br/>It's not so much a "horror" story per se, with most of the true horror being in Kawashima and Chiaki's mistreatment as children, and how it continues to warp and destroy their lives as adults - Kawashima's homicidal fantasies and Chiaki's self-destructiveness </span>
  <span id="freeText10371933274991294284" style="display:none"><i>This review and stranger things on <a href="https://bloodredvelvet.wordpress.com/category/book-reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Red Velvet</a>.</i><br /><br />Some books are unrelenting rays of sunshine, filling you with joy, optimism and hope for the future..... and then there is <i>Piercing</i>, a two-hundred-page miasma of darkness and human misery.<br /><br />It's not so much a "horror" story per se, with most of the true horror being in Kawashima and Chiaki's mistreatment as children, and how it continues to warp and destroy their lives as adults - Kawashima's homicidal fantasies and Chiaki's self-destructiveness collide into a corrosive mess after they meet by chance.<br /><br /> There are a lot of parallels to his earlier book, <i>Coin Locker Babies</i> in that the characters have a lot of pent-up rage and agony from childhood that never could be vented or gotten justice for.<br />Ryu (not Haruki, do not confuse them) Murakami's artistic writing style, with its fractured pacing, is like a bandage being torn off slowly and with a great deal of tension, as if you're not sure whether it will reveal a gaping wound or a small cut. Ultimately, it is both - <i>Piercing</i> paints a portrait of a wound which seems small on the surface, but runs bone-deep.<br /><br />**Contains some content that could be disturbing or triggering, namely depictions of abuse and self-harm.**</span>
  <a data-text-id="10371933274991294284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_238323130" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238323130" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238323130?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780747582205" href="/book/show/818121.Piercing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=lit">lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=black-as-night">black-as-night</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=translation">translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238323130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12674077081485995137"><div>
  <br/>
  <a href='http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ryVWnWV3a3Y/ULU9lUqPhuI/AAAAAAAACw4/tmb49iBjr8k/s1600/Piercing+Ryu+Murakami.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img alt='' height='640' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363590i/715025._SY540_.jpg' width='508' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/818121.Piercing' rel='nofollow noopener'>Piercing</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8881.Ry_Murakami' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ryū Murakami</a><br/><br/>My rating: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238323130' rel='nofollow noopener'>4 of 5 stars</a><br/><br/><br/><b>Blurb:</b> In Piercing, Murakami, in his own unique style, explores themes of child abuse and what happens to the voiceless among us, weaving a disturbing, spare tale of two people who find each other and then are forced into hurting each other deeply because of the haunting specter of their own abuse as children.<i> </i>Piercing is set in Tokyo and follows Kawashima Masayuki trying to come to terms with his overwhelming desire to stab his infan</span>
  <span id="freeText12674077081485995137" style="display:none"><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ryVWnWV3a3Y/ULU9lUqPhuI/AAAAAAAACw4/tmb49iBjr8k/s1600/Piercing+Ryu+Murakami.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="" height="640" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363590i/715025._SY540_.jpg" width="508" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/818121.Piercing" rel="nofollow noopener">Piercing</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8881.Ry_Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Ryū Murakami</a><br><br>My rating: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238323130" rel="nofollow noopener">4 of 5 stars</a><br><br><br><b>Blurb:</b> In Piercing, Murakami, in his own unique style, explores themes of child abuse and what happens to the voiceless among us, weaving a disturbing, spare tale of two people who find each other and then are forced into hurting each other deeply because of the haunting specter of their own abuse as children.<i> </i>Piercing is set in Tokyo and follows Kawashima Masayuki trying to come to terms with his overwhelming desire to stab his infant child with an Ice Pick. He resolves to divert the impulse into an unsuspecting prostitute. However as he begins to execute his meticulous crime everything, including his past, begins to unravel.<br><br><b>Thoughts:</b> This was a seriously dark read. I'm not sure if you can really call Piercing an enjoyable read in the traditional sense but as with my previous Ryu Murakami experience this trip in to the world of two damaged little fuckers was incredibly satisfying.<br><blockquote>
<br><em>"Ten nights ago. He was in the bathtub with the baby, having just finished washing her. He handed her over to Yoko, who was waiting with a fluffy bath towel, and then he leaned back in the tub, leaving the pebbled-glass shower door partially open. Yoko was murmuring to the baby as she dried her, and he was aware of himself smiling at them. And then, with no prelude or warning, a thought came percolating up into his brain and he felt the muscles of his cheeks twitch and freeze.<br><br>'I wouldn’t ever stab that baby with an ice pick, would I?'</em> "</blockquote><br>The content is at times quite disturbing in it's descriptions of physical torture but possibly even more disturbing is the empathy and compassion you find yourself feeling for these two people who are clearly not entirely sane. Whilst this literary descent in to a nightmare world has the potential to be gore-filled the prose is actually restrained, using it's language sparingly to convey maximum effect and grim imagery. This is horror but not as we ordinarily consider it.<br><br>The writing of The Other Murakami is something wonderful to immerse yourself in and so very impressive for that very reason. Any moment I had to stop reading I found myself constantly thinking about the characters and the situation they were in, almost desperate to go back to it and find out what would happen.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <i>“In heated rooms, he often felt the outlines of his body, the border between him and the external world, grow disturbingly fuzzy.” </i>
</blockquote><br>It's a nerve shredding, adrenaline rush of a novel that leaves you turning the page in eager anticipation and whilst I cannot recommend this for everyone because of the hard to swallow content I feel it is something that deserves to be read by anyone not easily offended.<br><br>World cinema fans will know what it is like to experience the dark imagination of Ryu Murakami already; he is the author of Audition, the novel that Takashi Miike adapted for his shocking and disturbing movie of the same name, and whilst Piercing is not at that same level it still packs a real punch on multiple levels. I would highly recommend this to anyone looking to explore their literary boundaries and suggest following it up with the even more impressive <i>In The Miso Soup</i>. <br><br><u>
  <b>Further Viewing Suggestions:</b>
</u><br><a href="http://letterboxd.com/film/audition/" rel="nofollow noopener">Audition</a><br><a href="http://letterboxd.com/film/american-psycho/" rel="nofollow noopener">American Psycho</a><br><a href="http://letterboxd.com/film/lost-highway/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost Highway</a><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jyAchn39u9o/ULVEztcKD2I/AAAAAAAACzs/1w7Vh_6QLiU/s1600/Audition+American+Psycho+Lost+Highway.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="" height="360" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363590i/715026._SX540_.jpg" width="640" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Additional Reading:</b>
</u><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17810.In_the_Miso_Soup" rel="nofollow noopener">In The Miso Soup</a> by Ryu Murakami<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25365.Out" rel="nofollow noopener">Out</a> by Natsuo Kirino<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/884085.Requiem_for_a_Dream" rel="nofollow noopener">Requiem For A Dream</a> by Hubert Selby Jr.<br><div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647820686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6460900132656988939">so this book made me feel physically unwell. I think it was an excellent, well-written book, masterfully translated, but it was extremely painful and unpleasant to read. <br/><br/>the two main characters have a lot of residual damage from childhood traumas that they never dealt with. it's a very visceral, intense and dark story. murakami's descriptions of violence and abuse are graphic and minutely detailed, but not without compassion. the characters are fully realized, and I think the characters' relentl</span>
  <span id="freeText6460900132656988939" style="display:none">so this book made me feel physically unwell. I think it was an excellent, well-written book, masterfully translated, but it was extremely painful and unpleasant to read. <br /><br />the two main characters have a lot of residual damage from childhood traumas that they never dealt with. it's a very visceral, intense and dark story. murakami's descriptions of violence and abuse are graphic and minutely detailed, but not without compassion. the characters are fully realized, and I think the characters' relentless battering of themselves and each other was so overwhelming that their disturbed thoughts became more compelling and, in a way, understandable (compulsive self-mutilation, for example, or how masayuki learned to isolate himself from pain and fear kindness). <br /><br />there were also some important points about how precarious your life is when you're part of a marginalized group, like immigrants or sex workers. <br /><br />seriously doubt I would ever even entertain the idea of reading this again, and I don't know if I'll ever read anything else by ryu "the other" murakami. but I think it's very powerful and worth reading, if you can stomach it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6460900132656988939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2176657695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176657695" />
    <a title="Wasee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11785803-wasee"><img alt="Wasee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588055892p2/11785803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176657695?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wasee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wasee" href="/user/show/11785803-wasee">Wasee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747593133" href="/book/show/830979.Piercing">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176657695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18242995772567610974">Memories aren't like words; they're soft and gooey. Covered with a sticky slime, like a penis after sex, or a vagina when you menstruate, and shaped like tadpoles or tiny watersnakes. When these sleeping memories are awakened, they begin to squirm and then swim, slowly at first but gradually faster, up to the surface. And once they get there, your senses shut down. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360353326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360353326" />
    <a title="Ruby  Tombstone [With A Vengeance]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance"><img alt="Ruby  Tombstone [With A Vengeance]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444744872p2/5973086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360353326?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruby  Tombstone [With A Vengeance]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruby  Tombstone [With A Vengeance]" href="/user/show/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance">Ruby  Tombstone [With A Vengeance]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance?shelf=littry-fikshun">littry-fikshun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance?shelf=creepy-kooky-and-or-spooky">creepy-kooky-and-or-spooky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973086-ruby-tombstone-with-a-vengeance?shelf=east-and-south-east-asia">east-and-south-east-asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360353326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7793660330669841437">This is a stunningly good book that mixes visceral and disturbing psychological landscapes with an extremely intelligent, almost farcical story structure. I have never read anything quite like it.<br/><br/>The two main characters (and there really are only two characters in this rather short book) are both acutely damaged from childhood trauma and abuse. Each sees the world in an entirely different way, and each perceives the other's actions through a lens of their own psychological damage. This leads to </span>
  <span id="freeText7793660330669841437" style="display:none">This is a stunningly good book that mixes visceral and disturbing psychological landscapes with an extremely intelligent, almost farcical story structure. I have never read anything quite like it.<br /><br />The two main characters (and there really are only two characters in this rather short book) are both acutely damaged from childhood trauma and abuse. Each sees the world in an entirely different way, and each perceives the other's actions through a lens of their own psychological damage. This leads to an almost comical and certainly suspenseful, continual escalation of events that you feel can only ever end in disaster. <br /><br />The way "The Other Murakami" writes about the effects of abuse is detailed, specific, unflinching, matter-of-fact and yet extremely visceral. Murakami gives the reader a sense of the utter physicality of mental health issues. There's a recognition that it's not just a matter of having unhealthy thoughts, but that these issues have physical elements: sweating and dizziness, the sound of blood rushing in ears...... I have the strong feeling that only someone who has been through some extreme trauma themselves could have written this. It's an uncomfortable feeling, but that's a large part of what gives this book such impact.<br /><br />It's a short book, it's not heavy-going, and it's brilliant. What are you waiting for?</span>
  <a data-text-id="7793660330669841437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1156910587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156910587" />
    <a title="Romina Nicolaides" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25129938-romina-nicolaides"><img alt="Romina Nicolaides" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442987660p2/25129938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156910587?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romina Nicolaides" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romina Nicolaides" href="/user/show/25129938-romina-nicolaides">Romina Nicolaides</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25129938-romina-nicolaides?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156910587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14722014712422770694">Piercing is a short and poignant book about a seemingly balanced family man who after some sleepless nights realizes he has raging fantasies about stabbing his baby girl with an ice pick. In order to avoid this fate he decides he needs to focus his attention somewhere else and concludes that the best avenue for his drive is to stab a woman. He gives his wife and company an excuse, takes the week off work and settles into a hotel in the business district where prostitutes abound. <br/><br/>He plans the mur</span>
  <span id="freeText14722014712422770694" style="display:none">Piercing is a short and poignant book about a seemingly balanced family man who after some sleepless nights realizes he has raging fantasies about stabbing his baby girl with an ice pick. In order to avoid this fate he decides he needs to focus his attention somewhere else and concludes that the best avenue for his drive is to stab a woman. He gives his wife and company an excuse, takes the week off work and settles into a hotel in the business district where prostitutes abound. <br /><br />He plans the murder meticulously and after a quick test run he puts his plan in motion. Right from the start and while he tries to order things in his mind we find that far from the balanced individual Kawashima is a deeply troubled person who is plagued by a rather dark past initiated by an abusive mother. <br /><br />On the day of the plan Kawashima orders a prostitute to his room and everything that could go wrong does. In a fated twist, his intended victim is quite unpredictable and puts several dents in his plan as the night unfolds. I won’t add spoilers this time, but suffice it to say that Murakami writes both of the characters in this book masterfully and explores their off kilter psychological universes so brilliantly that you would never question the veracity of their souls. <br /><br />Though I’ve read a lot of horror and similar genres I can honestly say this book was one of the most deeply disturbing yet thoroughly enjoyable reads I’ve experienced. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14722014712422770694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_875280138" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer875280138&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer875280138" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8353380255112205888">I actually like Ryu Murakami most of the time, but this book was just, like, a parody of himself. Starts out with a guy messing around with his baby's cheek with an ice pick while his wife is sleeping behind him, thinking how nice a guy he is for not killing the baby, then he decides he needs to stab the ice pick into some woman's stomach, then decides on top of that he needs to know first hand if a sliced Achilles tendon really makes a loud pop, then gets a love hotel and writes all this down i</span>
  <span id="freeText8353380255112205888" style="display:none">I actually like Ryu Murakami most of the time, but this book was just, like, a parody of himself. Starts out with a guy messing around with his baby's cheek with an ice pick while his wife is sleeping behind him, thinking how nice a guy he is for not killing the baby, then he decides he needs to stab the ice pick into some woman's stomach, then decides on top of that he needs to know first hand if a sliced Achilles tendon really makes a loud pop, then gets a love hotel and writes all this down in a notebook and calls a special massage girl, but she happens to also be fucked up and stabs herself in the leg repeatedly with a pair of small scissors, they go to the hospital to get stitched up, then to her apartment. She tries to put him to sleep with GHB or something like that, but before he sleeps he manages to tie her up with electrical cord, then he passes out, she gets out of the cord, cleans up, and the guy wakes up and leaves. <br /><br />There, I just told you the entire book.<br /><br />So cliché, that Japanese stereotype of senseless, creepy violence, like the Guinea Pig movies, etc. This was a big turd of a book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8353380255112205888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6711587281258960372">One of the most delightfully fucked up books I have ever read is Piercing. Yet, despite its gruesome content (Psychopathic killer vs Schizophrenic Prostitute) there is a strange and beautiful philosophy delicately balanced between the two protagonists. I must say that the strangeness of the tale does have the unique flavoring of the Japanese, so those who are fond of Japanese writing will probably like this.   <span id="freeText6711587281258960372" style="display:none">One of the most delightfully fucked up books I have ever read is Piercing. Yet, despite its gruesome content (Psychopathic killer vs Schizophrenic Prostitute) there is a strange and beautiful philosophy delicately balanced between the two protagonists. I must say that the strangeness of the tale does have the unique flavoring of the Japanese, so those who are fond of Japanese writing will probably like this. However, for those of you who enjoy the neat, though often exciting bundles of Western writing, you will likely be completely weirded out and confused by this. It does not follow Western conventions or expectations which is partly why I enjoyed it so much, but it is definitely not for everyone. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4634947576298145790">A father feels a nightly compulsion to stab his infant daughter with an ice pick. To avoid murdering his child, he tells his wife he's going on a business trip and decides to stab a prostitute instead. <br/><br/>Are you still with me? Good.<br/><br/>It turns out the prostitute is just as twisted and it sets up a very strange evening as the two psychos confront each other as well as the demons of their pasts. <br/><br/>This is a short read with short chapters, until the prostitute shows up and in an appropriate move, the enco</span>
  <span id="freeText4634947576298145790" style="display:none">A father feels a nightly compulsion to stab his infant daughter with an ice pick. To avoid murdering his child, he tells his wife he's going on a business trip and decides to stab a prostitute instead. <br /><br />Are you still with me? Good.<br /><br />It turns out the prostitute is just as twisted and it sets up a very strange evening as the two psychos confront each other as well as the demons of their pasts. <br /><br />This is a short read with short chapters, until the prostitute shows up and in an appropriate move, the encounter is captured in one 100-page chapter of nonstop action and madness. Brilliant pacing and a David Lynchian surrealist scenario make Piercing one of the most interesting and strangest books I've read in a while. If you can handle a few triggers, this one is well worth your time. I'll read Ryu Murakami's cult classic In the Miso Soup next.</span>

<div id="review_119434445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119434445" />
    <a title="christa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40816-christa"><img alt="christa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349499447p2/40816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119434445?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="christa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="christa" href="/user/show/40816-christa">christa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119434445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11089866885841531597">It has probably been two years since I read “In the Miso Soup,” what I consider more than just Ryu Murakami's flagship novel, but one of the few pieces of literature that I still draw on regularly when I want to ush and gush about fiction. I can still conjure what it feels like to read that book: Dreamy, terrifying and lonely, with a touch of nausea. And whenever I get into a conversation about books with someone I know can handle the dankest of dank, and the sourest of sour, the bloodiest of bl</span>
  <span id="freeText11089866885841531597" style="display:none">It has probably been two years since I read “In the Miso Soup,” what I consider more than just Ryu Murakami's flagship novel, but one of the few pieces of literature that I still draw on regularly when I want to ush and gush about fiction. I can still conjure what it feels like to read that book: Dreamy, terrifying and lonely, with a touch of nausea. And whenever I get into a conversation about books with someone I know can handle the dankest of dank, and the sourest of sour, the bloodiest of bloody – something that should be packaged with it's own air sickness bag -- I recommend it. <br /><br />Since then, I've been working my way through his canon, but cannot find another instance of where Murakami gives the literary equivalent of a kidney chop like he did in “Miso Soup.” “Piercing,” which was the followup to the greatest book of all time has moments of sublimely ishy text, but just doesn't have plot flow that it requires. It's like using fresh ingredients on day-old bread. Or, in this case, using freshly sanitized puncturing tools on a seasoned cutter. <br /><br />Murakami gets to the grit on impact, with Kawashima Masayuki watching his newborn daughter asleep in her crib in the middle of the night. Within three pages, he is caressing her cheek with an ice pick. Imagining what it would feel like to puncture the baby's skin. Instead of following his brutal instincts, he makes himself a promise: He will instead stab a prostitute with the ice pick. Get it out of his system, and save his little family. Kawashima begins filling a notebook with elaborate plans involving gloves, a change of clothes, a falsified accent, and the size, shape and skin color of the victim. <br /><br />“The woman must be not only young, but petite. A large woman would be more difficult to control in the event of any unforeseen glitches,” he writes after a dry-run with an aged masseuse. <br /><br />Turns out this isn't the first time that Kawashima has experienced such a craving. While he has gone on to become a successful graphic designer, a father, the husband of a woman who teaches classes in bread and pastry making in their home, he has had a troubled past. Abused, neglected, eventually raised by a foster family. When he was in his late teens, he got embroiled in a relationship with an older woman. A stripper old enough to sometimes mistaken for his mother, and who openly mocked him by bringing home strange men. One night, in a snit, Kawashima stabbed that woman in the stomach with an ice pick. The police were never involved. The woman lived. They broke up, but she did tell him that it really hurt during a few conversations they had in the aftermath. <br /><br />When he makes the call to the escort service, Sanada Chiaki's perspective comes into play. The young OCD prostitute is a self-mutilator who has recently misplaced her sex drive. She's got her own tales to tell, and when it finally comes down to go-time, things fail to follow the plans Kawashima sketched out so carefully. <br /><br />Murakami – a Japanese novelist, musician, TV talk show host – still manages to write better-than average fiction even at his worst. He creates worlds that look normal on the outside, but when you lift the lid you find it oozing with lawlessness. Well dressed sociopaths camouflaged with manners and hygiene, and bystanders who don't just turn a blind eye – they don't pay close enough attention to notice that anything might be amiss in the first place. <br /><br />This one is filled with black humor and picturesque words, but the apex of the novel is long with frequent perspective shifts that make it a little clunky. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11089866885841531597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1331769865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Scott Brook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7801535-scott-brook"><img alt="Scott Brook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329899582p2/7801535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Brook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Brook" href="/user/show/7801535-scott-brook">Scott Brook</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1331769865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer604446137178594045">A nice quick read, although with a rather dark and sadistic tone. The plot is rather simple. A damaged man with an urge to kill picks his first victim not knowing that she is just as or even more damaged. Cat and mouse ensues. Worth a read. However, if the reader has weak stomach, I would not recommend doing this while eating, as I did. Some pretty graphic depictions are included.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3298789127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_167608438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167608438" />
    <a title="Ernest Junius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2978878-ernest-junius"><img alt="Ernest Junius" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594545696p2/2978878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167608438?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ernest Junius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ernest Junius" href="/user/show/2978878-ernest-junius">Ernest Junius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747593133" href="/book/show/830979.Piercing">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">porn filmmakers, psychologist</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=books-that-took-forever-to-finish">books-that-took-forever-to-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=shallow-reads">shallow-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=cool-books">cool-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167608438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9149286778543805589">I don't know if it was because of my overwhelming work flow in the office these 2 weeks, I only managed to finish this book after 10 days or more. It shouldn't be that way though, since <i>Piercing</i> is relatively thin and easy to read.<br/><br/>The only reason I can come up with, for reading it for far too long, is that it doesn't has its usual Murakami grip, as what I felt in <i>In The Miso Soup</i> and <i>Audition</i>.<br/><br/>It began pretty interesting, a quest of a somebody whose objective is to get rid of his fear, which he a</span>
  <span id="freeText9149286778543805589" style="display:none">I don't know if it was because of my overwhelming work flow in the office these 2 weeks, I only managed to finish this book after 10 days or more. It shouldn't be that way though, since <i>Piercing</i> is relatively thin and easy to read.<br /><br />The only reason I can come up with, for reading it for far too long, is that it doesn't has its usual Murakami grip, as what I felt in <i>In The Miso Soup</i> and <i>Audition</i>.<br /><br />It began pretty interesting, a quest of a somebody whose objective is to get rid of his fear, which he assumed can be achieved by stabbing a girl in the stomach with an icepick and severing her achilles tendon (which according to the book will produce a sound that is similar to a gun shot). As the story developed the protagonist trapped in a situation where he couldn't just kill his victim—a young prostitute—yet. And there developed drama and twists, which exposed the battle of wits and psychoanalysis of two deranged minds.<br /><br />I love the plot, I like it. It's witty and dark. It is very Ryu Murakami to write something like that. What's more in this, though, Murakami explored more about sexuality and perversion (ball gag, sheer purple panties, whip, blood, swiss army knife, stockings, and more), which I too find every insightful.<br /><br />The downside of it come with the lack of details behind the characters' mental state of mind. It's not like Murakami didn't explain at all what's behind the deranged minds. He gave the small parts of the information, but he kept the big parts uncovered. It is like when your friend says, <br />"hey I got this secret... it's about A..."<br />"what, what?"<br />"ah! I forget, I am not supposed to tell you..."<br />Then she left with a big grin on her face.<br /><br />It is a little bit annoying really.<br /><br />Also <i>Piercing</i> seemed to be written clumsily, leaving logical gaffes here and there, although they might be debatable. But what I wanted to say is, that it is not solid. Not only that, the conversations between the characters also feel a little bit artificial and fabricated—it is not as natural. Maybe this is Murakami's worst yet... but still he wrote it with efficiency above normal fiction novels, which deserved praise. <br /><br />I think this work is an effigy of Murakami's sexual drive and passion. It treads somewhere between pornography and BDSM. If this was a movie, this could be mistaken as an JAV—which also might work too. <br /><br />Anyway, weighing all the pros and cons, I would still recommend <i>Piercing</i> for those who want to learn more about Japan's sexual state of mind. It could be very interesting to know. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9149286778543805589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
